Wang Jingwei Will Go to Beijing Soon 114

Expressing Agreement with Chiang Kai-shek's Three Points

After President Wang Jingwei of the Executive Yuan resigned, he was repeatedly and earnestly retained by various Central Committee members. Although he did not agree to withdraw his resignation, he indicated that he would return to Beijing soon. The information obtained by the Central News Agency reporter yesterday is recorded as follows:

Wang Jingwei's Whereabouts: Wang Jingwei returned to his private residence on Xipushi Road at around 6:00 AM yesterday morning. At around 7:00 AM, Tang Youren, Secretary-General of the Central Political Council, visited him and talked for a long time. At around 10:00 AM, Wang Jingwei secretly went out alone again and returned home in about 20 minutes. At around 11:00 AM, Tang Youren met with journalists at Wang's residence, and Wang Jingwei left the residence through the side door on the east side at this time. He did not return home until around 1:00 PM. At around 2:00 PM, he met with Zhang Dingfan, former Mayor of Shanghai, and at 5:00 PM, he met with Chen Gongbo, Minister of Industry.

Tang Youren's Remarks: At 11:00 AM yesterday morning, Tang Youren, Secretary-General of the Central Political Council, hosted reporters at Wang's residence. According to him, he received a telegram from Chairman Chiang on the evening of the 9th and flew to Wuhan to see Chiang on the morning of the 10th. Chiang Kai-shek was quite concerned about Wang Jingwei's sudden resignation and inquired in detail about the reasons for Wang's resignation. After Tang Youren informed him of the facts, Chiang Kai-shek immediately expressed the following three points: (1) He agreed to approve Director Zhang Xueliang's resignation from Beiping; (2) He firmly retained President Wang from resigning; (3) He hoped that President Wang would go to Lushan to discuss everything. After Tang Youren returned to Shanghai on the 11th, he reported the visit to Wuhan and Chiang Kai-shek's three points in detail to President Wang. However, President Wang's intention to resign remained firm. Tang Youren then telegraphed Chiang Kai-shek, detailing Wang's continued insistence on resigning. Chiang Kai-shek believed that in this time of national crisis, the central government should not be without a person in charge for a day. Wu Zhihui, a Central Committee member, happened to be going to Wuhan, so he entrusted Wu to carry a personal letter from Chiang to Wang to Shanghai. Wu arrived in Shanghai yesterday (i.e., the day before yesterday) afternoon. After Wu arrived in Shanghai, he and Finance Minister Song Ziwen, Army Commander He Yingqin, Education Minister Zhu Jiahua, and Director Zhu Peide visited Wang at Xipushi Road at 5:00 PM yesterday (i.e., the day before yesterday). Wu presented Chiang's personal letter to President Wang. The letter was very long and its main points were: (1) Zhang Xueliang's resignation is not a problem, but the military affairs in North China are heavy, and there should be considerable preparation before Zhang's resignation; (2) The resignation of the President of the Executive Yuan is of great importance and cannot be resolved by a few Central Committee members in Shanghai discussing it or exchanging telegrams. Therefore, please go to Lushan to meet with Chairman Lin Sen in order to discuss everything with him. Chairman Lin also intends to invite Wang to Lushan for consultations. Chiang Kai-shek also sent a separate telegram to Wang, inviting him to Lushan, and telegraphed each Minister, including He, Zhu, and Song, asking them to make earnest persuasions when meeting with President Wang. Wang Jingwei expressed agreement with the points in Chiang Kai-shek's letter and indicated that he would go to Beijing after the issue of Director Zhang's resignation was resolved. Tang Youren also told reporters on the phone last night that the date of Wang's visit to Beijing has not been determined. It is still unknown whether it will happen the day after tomorrow.

Chen Gongbo's Remarks: Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo came to Shanghai the night before last and had contact with President Wang. Chen visited Wang yesterday morning, and Wang invited Chen to lunch at a garden in western Shanghai at noon. After two talks, the results were very satisfactory. At around 4:00 PM in the afternoon, Chen left Wang's residence and told reporters from the Central News Agency that the Standing Committee of the Central Committee had approved the resignation of Zhang Xueliang, Pacification Commissioner of Beiping, and that President Wang would go to Beijing in a day or two. Chen himself returned to Beijing by overnight train last night.

Ma Zhanshan's Representative Talks About Ma's Determination to Resist Long-Term 115

Unless the Japanese Invaders are Driven Out of Our Territory

I Will Never Return Alive to See My Countrymen

Tian Xiuqiao, the representative of General Ma Zhanshan, Chairman of Heilongjiang Province, departed from Dongxingzhen, Bayan County, Heilongjiang Province on July 29th, arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday, reported the situation of the Anti-Japanese War of the Heilongjiang Army to all circles, and scheduled to go to Beijing soon to request the central government to send troops to recover the lost territory as soon as possible. Representative Tian is a graduate of the Japanese Army Non-commissioned Officer School and is currently the commander of the Fifth Regiment of the Second Cavalry Brigade of Heilongjiang, a brave soldier in the Anti-Japanese War in Northeast China. When reporters met with Representative Tian at the hotel yesterday, they inquired about the latest situation of the Anti-Japanese War in Northeast China. Mr. Wu Huanzhang, Director of the Heilongjiang Provincial Party Affairs Guidance Committee, was also present and informed reporters in detail about the current situation of the Party, government, and army in Heilongjiang Province. The conversation between the two is recorded below.

Tian Xiuqiao's Talk 116

For several weeks, news of the Black Army has been scarce, mainly because of malfunctions in the military shortwave radio. The Japanese side has seized the opportunity to spread rumors, disrupting information. They claim that Chairman Ma has been killed in battle or that the Black Army has suffered various defeats. These are the usual tricks of clowns and not worth a laugh. However, this also reveals the general "admiration, envy, and fear" that the Japanese hold for our Chairman Ma, who is sincerely patriotic and determined to resist Japan. Since our army began resisting Japan, it has received much praise and assistance from the people, especially from various circles in Shanghai and overseas Chinese. Chairman Ma, fearing that the people might be worried, specially sent his brother south to report on the Black Army's resistance against Japan and to urge the central government to send troops as soon as possible to annihilate the Japanese invaders, recover lost territory, and rescue the 30 million people of Northeast China from their dire situation, thus relieving their suffering.

For months, Japanese aircraft have been showing off their might. Not a day goes by without the Black Army fighting the Japanese. Here is a brief overview to inform the people: The Black Army fought the Japanese south of Hulan for more than 20 days. The soldiers fought bravely, each fighting for himself. With a single cry, each man was ready to take on a hundred. Therefore, they repeatedly defeated the enemy, who fled in panic, building strong fortifications and not daring to cross the line. Our side was planning to take advantage of the situation and annihilate them, but the enemy changed its strategy, repeatedly using more than 20 heavy bombers to bomb Hailun, Suihua, Hulan, and other prosperous counties in our Black province. The people suffered countless deaths and injuries, and countless houses collapsed in a truly unbearable scene. Our army suffered losses due to the lack of anti-aircraft weapons. To protect our compatriots and preserve our strength, we had to voluntarily abandon the cities and move to the countryside to continue fighting the Japanese. The Japanese, fearing our encirclement, did not dare to enter the cities to burn, kill, and loot. This was a win-win strategy.

Chairman Ma intended to contact Commander Ding and Commander Li on June 20, seeking a large-scale offensive, and moved towards Shangji Chang, Qingcheng, Bayan, and other places, defeating the Japanese troops there. Our army then occupied the Daqingshan area as a base for long-term resistance. Daqingshan is a natural fortress, where "one man can hold the pass against ten thousand." Our army can also hide in forests that have not been harvested for thousands of years, hearing voices but not seeing people, able to attack and defend. The Japanese army is currently at a loss. Although they have recently used aircraft to reconnoiter and drop bombs, it has been ineffective. Now, the Japanese artillery fire cannot reach, the bombs cannot be used, and their plans have been exhausted. The troops led by our Chairman Ma are all exceptionally brave and skilled. They include the First Brigade under Wu Songlin, the Second Brigade under Liang Zhenduo, the Third Brigade under Bu Fuchen, the Fourth Brigade under Deng Wen, and the Seventh Brigade under Cai Hongyou, totaling more than 40,000 men. Brigade Commander Liang of the Second Brigade also serves as the commander-in-chief of the militia, commanding more than 30,000 men, all of whom are well-equipped with firearms and are Northeast warriors who have sworn to defend their country and fight the enemy to the death. Only the lack of ammunition is a regrettable issue.

Although the Japanese army fears our Chairman Ma like a deity and hates him to the bone, their ambition has not died. Therefore, on July 14, the Japanese 14th Division and part of the 8th Division used field artillery and aircraft to cover infantry and cavalry, launching a fierce general attack on our Chen garrison in four bloody battles lasting six days and nights. Our army, facing a matter of life and death, firmly defended the Chen garrison and fought desperately. The arrogant Japanese army was finally defeated. The intensity of the battle surpassed even the Jiangqiao battle last year. In this battle, the Japanese suffered about 1,000 casualties, with corpses strewn across the fields. Those not burned by themselves rotted and smelled terrible. Chairman Ma, to uphold humanity, ordered that they all be buried at the foot of the mountain. Our army also suffered heavy casualties. After suffering this setback, the Japanese army dared not act rashly and changed its strategy, adopting a policy of encirclement and blockade. Our army had long anticipated the enemy's plan and hid in the forests or lurked in the green crops. At night, they launched surprise attacks on the enemy's encampments and used small units to attack and harass the enemy's large units, avoiding direct conflict. When they attacked, we retreated; when they retreated, we attacked. The Japanese army struggled to cope and was exhausted. With the rise of the green crops, the overflowing rivers, and the blocked transportation in the mountain area, and with mosquitoes eating people, the Japanese army suffered even more. Around July 25, they withdrew completely to the Hu-Hai line, their intentions unclear.

Chairman Ma is determined. Chairman Ma travels day and night, supervising his subordinates without the slightest懈怠, and is more energetic than before. He often says to those around him, "I (Ma referring to himself) live in prosperous cities, enjoying ease and leisure, but I feel depressed and sluggish. Every time I eat and sleep in the open, riding a horse and galloping amidst the sounds of battle, I feel refreshed and invigorated. Now, fighting the Japanese bandits in the mountain area, I am fighting for the dignity of my 400 million compatriots and for the glory of the Republic of China. I have long disregarded life and death and do not feel that my situation is difficult. There is nothing difficult in the world; it all depends on the firmness of one's determination." Chairman Ma also often goes to various units to instruct and encourage his subordinates to vow to defend the country and to fulfill their duties as soldiers, even if they fight to their last bullet and last soldier, and to not return to see their countrymen until they drive the Japanese bandits out of the country. His subordinate officers and soldiers, mindful of the country's dire situation, all voluntarily forgo their salaries and save them to purchase ammunition. Although they are now in the countryside, their morale is as high as ever, and they have pledged to fight the enemy to the death to save the country and to deal with the Japanese bandits to the end.

I earnestly hope for reinforcements. At the moment, although our army lacks ammunition, this is not yet a major concern. What we fear is that the enemy's reinforcements are constantly arriving and increasing daily, while we have no assistance of a single soldier, a single arrow, or a single bullet. If this continues for a long time, and the enemy's foundation becomes solid, then our 30 million people in Northeast China will die without a place to be buried, and their property will be beyond saving. Let us not dwell on past faults. Now, Director Zhang is emulating the lofty style of the ancients and has resolutely retired. We hope that the central government will quickly select and appoint wise and capable individuals to lead the brave soldiers of the Northeast, taking advantage of the fact that the green crops have not yet fallen and the volunteers are victorious, to break through the pass, recover lost territory, restore our homeland, and rescue our Northeast compatriots from their dire situation. Every person in Northeast China is willing to be a vanguard, devoting their lives to the battlefield. The recent actions of the volunteer army demonstrate the general mentality of our Northeast people.

Waiting for a general offensive. Commander Ding and Commander Li are currently in the Lingyuan and Jinkou areas, with more than 30,000 troops under their command. Commander Wang Delin is in Hengdaohezi, with more than 10,000 troops. Commander Feng Zhanhai is in Wuchang, with 7,000 troops. They have all joined forces and are waiting for a general offensive to annihilate the enemy in one fell swoop. They deeply hope that the people will provide rear support.

Wu Huanzhang's Talk 117

Wu Huanzhang, the guiding committee member of the Heilongjiang Province Party Affairs, previously went south for negotiations. Now that his mission is complete, he left Shanghai on the 5th of last month, heading to Heilongjiang via Vladivostok. However, upon arriving in that city, he was immediately detained by the Soviet Russian authorities and repeatedly interrogated. He was finally released on the 7th of this month and sent aboard the original ship to Shanghai. He arrived in port the day before yesterday. According to Wu, the Party, government, and military circles in Heilongjiang Province have united as one. The Party headquarters has formed a political department of the army, deeply involved in guiding the anti-Japanese movement among the people. The people of Heilongjiang Province are already armed and only need a little training to become a strong anti-Japanese force. He will head north within days to engage in this work.

Yun Huifang Released Amid Thunderous Applause 118

Judge Feng ruled to allow Yun's bail.

The police lawyer still insisted it was not possible.

The crowd cheered loudly when leaving the court.

Humanity is not dead; the treacherous merchants should be ashamed.

Yun Huifang, a patriotic youth, was arrested for warning treacherous merchants who were privately selling Japanese goods. The Second Special District Local Court sentenced her to two months imprisonment with a two-year reprieve. Subsequently, the Public Concession Police, citing the bombing of the Yongchang Coal Company on Xinzha Road by the Blood Soul Assassination Group, which injured Yu Ruiliang, and the bomb threat letters received by the Cotton Cloth Guild on Shanxi Road, also alleged to be committed by Yun Huifang and Cai Yaozu, requested the First Special District Local Court to prepare a document. On Thursday of the previous week, they went to the Second Special Court and brought Yun to the police station. They also searched Yun and Cai's residence at 207 Park Road, discovering a hand grenade. The next day, they were sent to the First Special Court, where police lawyer Ru Baoyi charged Yun under Articles 282 and 318 of the Criminal Law. After interrogation by Judge Feng Shide, the case was adjourned to a later date because the victim, Yu Ruiliang, did not appear. Yun Huifang's detention has been reported in this newspaper.

A continuous stream of listeners. Yesterday morning was the date for the continuation of the trial. The Chinese and foreign detectives in charge of the case escorted Yun to the First Criminal Court of the First Special Court at 8:30 AM. Both lawyers also appeared in court one after another. However, the Public Works Department, which filed the lawsuit, also sent the department's acting chief lawyer, Gan Jingxian, to participate. People from all walks of life came to court to listen, in an endless stream. After 9:00 AM, the court was already overcrowded, and the area outside the court was still extremely crowded, estimated to be around five or six hundred people.

Yu Ruiliang did not appear in court. At 9:30 AM, Judge Feng, Chief Prosecutor Wang, and the clerk took their seats. They ordered the bailiffs to bring the defendant to the defendant's box. First, lawyer Ru Baoyi stated that Yu Ruiliang had been summoned and had personally signed the summons, but he had not yet appeared. He did not know why. Then, Chinese detective No. 129 reported on the situation of summoning Yu at the Yongcheng Coal Company.

The Second Special Court did not appeal. Judge Feng then asked Yun Huifang, "How did the Second Special District Court rule on your case? What crime were you convicted of?" Yun replied, "They sentenced me to two months' imprisonment with a two-year reprieve." Lawyer Zhao Chen added, "The court made its judgment based on Article 319 of the Criminal Law." The judge continued to ask, "Did you or the plaintiff declare an appeal in that case?" Yun shook her head repeatedly. Lawyer Zhao replied that the police lawyer was very satisfied with the judgment at the time and did not advocate for an appeal.

Throwing the bomb was an entire plan. The judge asked, "What kind of actions did you take in that case?" Yun replied, "I also used a bomb to warn the treacherous merchant Maochang Foreign Cloth Company." The judge asked, "Was this action intended to warn all treacherous merchants with bombs, and was it part of an entire plan?" Yun immediately said, "Yes." Judge Feng then declared that the case had a continuing relationship with the case in the French Concession, so the court considered it necessary to review the case files. Because of this legal issue, the trial could not proceed today and would have to be postponed.

Photo of Yun Huifang (center) being released on bail from the courthouse (Photo by Li Zunyong) 119

Yun Huifang was granted bail by shop guarantee. Lawyer Li Zuyu immediately stood up and requested that the defendant be allowed to post bail. The judge nodded. At this time, police lawyer Gan Jingxian objected, saying that the case concerned local security, and the Public Works Department opposed bail. Lawyer Zhao Chen retorted that there was no need to object to this point. At this time, Judge Feng had already announced the ruling: the case was postponed for one week, pending the review of Yun Huifang's case files from the Second Special District Local Court. Yun Huifang was to be released on a substantial shop guarantee.

The police lawyer's appeal. Hearing this ruling, lawyer Gan continued to state that, according to Article 414 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, an appeal should be filed. Before this appeal was ruled on, he demanded that the execution of the bail ruling be suspended. Judge Feng immediately informed him that bail could not be appealed, while lawyer Li Zuyu stated that, according to Article 415 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, an appeal was not permitted. Lawyer Gan further stated that Article 420 of the Code of Criminal Procedure stipulated that the court could suspend execution before the appeal was ruled on. Lawyer Zhao Chen then rebutted, saying that the provision stated that it "may rule to suspend execution." Since the word "may" was used, it was clear that suspension was not mandatory. If the plaintiff was indeed dissatisfied, he could submit a written statement of opinion within three days according to Article 419.

The judge ordered the debate to end. Lawyer Gan continued, saying that the reason the police opposed bail was that the defendant was a member of the Blood Soul Group, and some accomplices had not yet been apprehended. If she were released on bail, there would be no hope of arresting the escaped accomplices, and there would still be a danger to security. Therefore, he had to oppose it. Lawyer Li Zuyu explained the purpose of detention in detail, saying that detention was intended to prevent escape and to facilitate the apprehension of accomplices. There was no need for detention beyond this. The defendant had been released on bail before and had not escaped. As for Cai, if he wanted to escape, he would not have to wait until the defendant was released on bail to escape. Therefore, the police's opposition to bail was an overreaction. At this point in the debate, the judge ruled that the case had been decided and ordered all parties to end the debate. He also ordered the police to take Yun to the bail office and allow her to be released on bail after the guarantee procedures were completed.

Two shops provided the guarantee. After the court granted bail, the listeners were overjoyed. The bailiff took her to the bail room to wait for bail. At that time, there were more than two hundred shops willing to provide a guarantee. Since the court only required a substantial shop guarantee, Baohe Tang on Sichuan Road and Xiangtai Silver Shop on Rue Robert were asked by Lawyer Zhao Chen to fill out the guarantee forms. Li Qianheng and Chen Shusheng from the two shops took out the seals they had prepared and stamped them, and signed their names to take responsibility. According to court practice, after filling out the guarantee form, it must be verified at the shop once. After going back and forth, the procedures were completed at half past twelve. Yun Huifang, amidst thunderous applause, followed Wang Jian'e and other representatives from the Changzhou Association in Shanghai, boarding car number 12032 and driving straight out of the courthouse door.

Yun Huifang's family history. According to Yun, her family has lived in Changzhou for generations. Her parents are both alive and well, but she has no brothers or sisters. Yun is the only one in the Yun lineage. She came to Shanghai to do business two years ago, initially working at the Minhua Printing House and recently joining the Lianhua Printing House on Shanhai Pass Road. Since this incident occurred, Lianhua has made no statement. She was treated very well in the police station and did not suffer any hardship, only asked to give a statement.

Matters of legal consideration will be discussed later.

While waiting for bail, the representatives of various groups who came to the court to listen planned to ask Yun to report on the situation at the police station to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce after she was released on bail. However, this proposal was dropped to avoid causing trouble. Before the case was opened, it was rumored that the court had held a meeting to discuss how to judge Yun's case. However, the reporter personally visited Judge Feng Shide, who replied that there was no such thing. However, before the trial, Judge Feng had discussed with police lawyer Ru Baoyi whether the offenses were legally connected. As a result, it was decided that the case files from the Second Special District Court would need to be retrieved for reference.

Yun will return to Changzhou for a short rest. As for Yun's whereabouts after leaving the court, it was kept secret to avoid patriotic comrades crowding to comfort her and to prevent opponents from harming her. It is said that she plans to return to her hometown of Changzhou to rest and await the court's trial.

The Public Works Department is on high alert. For the sake of protecting the peace of the court and maintaining order, the Public Works Department's police department specially dispatched a large team of armed detectives, thirty or forty men, driving a large red police car with a machine gun inside, to the front of the court, parked on the east side of North Zhejiang Road at Qipu Road. Some of the detectives in the car were deployed around the corridors inside the court gate to assist the existing bailiffs in maintaining security. All positions in the court were changed to double posts. The atmosphere at the time was quite tense, causing passersby who did not know the reason to stop and watch, but they all knew to maintain order, and there was no disorder throughout.

Leaving the court amidst cheers. Yun was in the judicial police office from 10:30 AM until 12:00 PM. The guarantee from the guarantor shop was submitted by the lawyer to Judge Feng for approval before she was allowed to regain her freedom. As soon as she left the threshold of the room, those who wanted to see the demeanor of the patriot, whether they knew her or not, rushed forward to express their condolences. Unexpectedly, Yun was surrounded. At that time, applause and cheers were heard in the distance. Several photographers also carried fast lenses and asked Yun to take a photo before representatives from various groups accompanied her to board the car, which drove away in cheers.

Large Numbers of Overseas Chinese Expelled from Japan Arrive in Shanghai 120

Overseas Chinese in Japan had successively returned to their home countries at the beginning of the war. Those who had not been able to return were generally people with economic difficulties and no work. The government had already transported three batches of them to Shanghai. Recently, there were still people stranded in Japan, with no means of livelihood, who were being pushed to Shanghai by the Japanese police. Yesterday, when the Kasado Maru ship arrived in Shanghai, another large group of Chinese were expelled. Here is a record of the situation:

Not allowed to stay in Japan. There was a group of Chinese workers in Yokkaichi, Mie Prefecture, Japan. Since the outbreak of the Shanghai War, they had been dismissed by Japanese factories. However, due to economic difficulties, they had not yet returned to their home countries. Now, the Japanese authorities, on the grounds that these Chinese workers did not have a certificate allowing them to stay in Japan and that they were subject to the ban on entry, should be expelled. The Nagoya Maritime Police Station took this large group of Chinese workers to the police station and detained them. On the 10th of this month, they were forced to board the Kasado Maru ship to Shanghai.

Number of people expelled. Those who were expelled by the Japanese maritime police and escorted to Shanghai included Zhu Jin Yan, Liu Chengfu, Zhuo Xishi, Xia Renxing, Ye Benfa, Ye Yansheng, Xu Xiangyan, Ding Yuanxiang, Ye Jinxiang, Zhou Zhongmei, Xu Zhengyuan, Xu Xiji, Mao Rongbiao, Chen Yuanfa, Liu Tuoyan, He Ruxing, Chen Nanxing, Wang Zuoxuan, Ye Zaolai, Wu Yueshu, Dong Yaoshu, Lin Keyuan, and Zhu Songbo, Zhang Lun, Chen Yihuo, and others, totaling thirty-four people.

Returning home in a state of distress. When those who were expelled arrived in Shanghai, they all landed at the Huishan Wharf. Each person's travel expenses had to be paid. If they did not have cash, they had to hand over their luggage to the ship to be kept by the Shanghai Japan Shipping Company. After they had collected the money, they could redeem it. Each person landed in Shanghai in a very distressed state. They have now all returned to their original homes in Wenzhou and Qingtian, Zhejiang.

The Baihe River is Blocked Again 121

The Xinming ran aground and was rescued.

After the Baihe River in Tianjin was blocked by silt, it was dredged by the Tianjin Customs this year, and Shanghai's Beiyang ships were able to pass through to Zizhulin. However, not long after the route reopened, on the 12th of this month, it was blocked again due to heavy upstream flooding. Ships with a draft of ten feet could not travel. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xinming ship, which had come to Shanghai from Tianjin, ran aground at the corner of the Baihe River Railway Pier on the 13th. The ship was trapped in the silt for two days and nights. Yesterday, a telegram was received stating that the Tianjin branch had sent a ship to tow it out. Whether the bottom of the ship was damaged or not needs to be inspected after arriving in Shanghai. From yesterday onwards, Chinese and foreign shipping companies in this port have again changed their Beiyang routes to end at Tanggu and will not go to Baihe Zizhulin. Passengers and cargo bound for Tianjin are all transferring ships in Tanggu.

The British-owned Public Bus Strike is Getting Worse 122

Armed escorts protect the reluctant operation of buses.

Yesterday, the No. 9 bus line was disrupted, affecting passengers.

The workers petitioned the Party and government agencies yesterday.

After the workers of the British-owned public bus company in the Public Concession went on strike, the striking workers adopted direct action, and unfortunate incidents occurred, and the situation deteriorated. The company announced the recruitment of new workers, and the provisional strike committee petitioned the Party and government agencies yesterday, requesting mediation. Details are recorded below:

Armed buses. After the company refused to negotiate, the workers adopted direct action, resulting in the beating of a White Russian, the blocking of buses, and the involvement of passengers the day before yesterday. The factory manager and superintendent of the company, specially for maintaining traffic, still dispatched fourteen buses on Route 1, seven buses on Route 2, seven buses on Route 5, six buses on Route 6, twenty-four buses on Route 9, and special express buses yesterday. Plainclothes Chinese police officers dispatched by the police station armed escorts to travel with the buses. At the same time, the police station notified all Chinese and foreign detectives to pay special attention and provide protection along the way to prevent incidents.

Passengers insulted. Although each bus route was protected by detectives yesterday, the striking workers still tried to block them. At 1:25 PM, No. 114 of Route 9, bus No. 97, sold No. 31, and Chinese police officer No. 4465, driving to the west of the Dongxin Bridge on Avenue Edward VII, were hit by striking workers throwing hollowed-out watermelons filled with manure from behind the bus. Eight Chinese passengers and two Western passengers were affected. The order was disrupted at once. The patrol officers used water to clean them. The British Chinese Public Bus Company agreed to be responsible for compensating for the damage to the passengers' clothing caused by the manure, and the matter was settled.

Recruiting new workers. The company is eager to find ways to restore the operation of public buses. Therefore, factory manager Xiao Date directly entrusted the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center to recruit new workers. Later, because the guidance center received a warning from the strike committee, it only recruited twenty-five people, who have already begun training. Yesterday, the company announced the qualifications for recruiting new workers: (1) able to read and speak English, (2) a suitable shop guarantee, (3) two two-inch photos (4) no addictions. Many people applied. The company's entrance on Connaught Road was overcrowded. These people knew that the strike committee would definitely try to make things difficult for them, but forced by livelihood, they disregarded everything and risked seeking employment. It can be seen that the panic of unemployment after the war is getting more and more serious, which is chilling.

Workers' congress. Public bus striking workers held a general assembly at the Renhe Teahouse on Wuding Road at 1:00 PM yesterday. The chairman first reported on the strike process and the company's refusal to negotiate. It was decided on the spot: (1) The six worker representatives designated by the company will have their status as strike committee members revoked. (2) Six people will be elected to supplement the strike committee. (3) A declaration will be issued with textual revisions. In a temporary motion, most workers advocated free action. After the strike committee explained everything and advised the crowd.

Strike committee statement. The strike committee said to the reporter of the New Voice Society yesterday that after the company refused the conditions, all the workers were extremely angry and advocated using force to deal with the company and destroying the vehicles. Because the workers came from the military and police, they were very confident. The strike committee repeatedly advised that the workers' strike was for their own lives and conditions. Absolutely do not take violent actions that affect passengers unless absolutely necessary. Only by consolidating unity, earnestly uniting the drivers, coppersmiths, sweepers, and Chinese staff, and fighting together can the four minimum requirements be resolved satisfactorily. There are absolutely no other excessive demands and actions. Moreover, this disturbance was not a strike committee order or resolution. It was caused by the company's oppression and should be the full responsibility of the company. The strike committee expressed its deep sympathy and regret for the passengers who were mistakenly affected.

Workers' petition. The provisional strike committee of the British-owned public bus company dispatched four representatives at 11:00 AM yesterday to petition the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, stating that the company had appointed ticket sellers Nos. 23, 133, 150, 208, 26, 3, 6, etc. on July 25 as worker representatives to negotiate wage increase plans in exchange for workers not taking bribes. However, the company did not fulfill its promise, suppressed the workers, and caused a strike. It was overthrown by force and dismissed. The third section mediator will receive them and promise to report to the director for handling. Later, he went to the Municipal Party Department to petition, where the director of the people's training section received him. He fully accepted the workers' request.

Petition to the Municipal Government by the Disaster Area Fire Insurance Compensation Advancement Association Regarding Compensation 123

During the outbreak of the January 28th Incident, Zhabei, Jiangwan, Wusong and other areas bore the brunt. Relying on their aircraft and artillery, the Japanese army wantonly bombed and burned our prosperous areas. Therefore, the losses of our people's houses and properties were enormous. After the armistice agreement was signed, the Japanese army gradually withdrew according to the procedures stipulated in the agreement. The disaster-avoiding people returned one after another, but their residences were burned and their property was robbed. The hardship of their situation could not be imagined by those who lived in the concessions. A portion of the residents, because they had fire insurance, negotiated with the companies, requesting compensation. However, a few companies believed that losses from military fire were not within the scope of fire insurance and that the company had no obligation to compensate. The policyholders believed that although some of the damage was caused by gunfire, most of it was caused by arson by the Japanese army and traitors. Therefore, it should be considered fire insurance. Because of this, the two sides were deadlocked and could not reach a decision for a long time. Recently, individual negotiations have felt scattered and it is feared that victory will be difficult to achieve. Therefore, more than 5,000 policyholders have organized the Shanghai Disaster Area Fire Insurance Compensation Advancement Association, elected committee members to negotiate with various companies, and obtained assistance from organizations such as the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Local Association, the Lawyers Association, and the Accountants Association, to organize research and uphold justice. After several meetings, the opinions of both parties were considered close. Unexpectedly, the insurance industry changed its mind midway, overturned the proposal, attempted to cancel the proposed issuance of public bonds, and refused to attend. The association was unable to proceed, so it sent more than 50 representatives, including Ye Jiaxing and Tang Youwei, to the municipal government yesterday afternoon at about 2:00 PM to petition. Five representatives were selected to enter and request to see Mayor Wu. The mayor was out on official business, so Municipal Government Secretary Wang Shaozhai received them on his behalf and promised to convey what the representatives said, along with the original petition, to the mayor and wait for instructions on how to handle it. The representatives were satisfied and left. Afterwards, according to those in charge of the municipal government, both sides in the Shanghai Incident had not declared war. Whether or not it can be called a war and whether the resulting losses are within the scope of fire insurance should be carefully studied. Moreover, this kind of dispute must be resolved through legal procedures and cannot be resolved by administrative action. However, what kind of reply and solution will be given must await the mayor's approval. After the representatives withdrew, they went to the Municipal Party Headquarters to petition. The association's document to the municipal government is recorded below: The document is presented to expose the insurance industry's pursuit of profit and disregard for the suffering of the disaster victims, and to present the whole story in detail, hoping that it will be reviewed and quickly given relief. Since the outbreak of the January 28th Incident, Zhabei, Jiangwan, and Wusong have been the hardest hit, all becoming war zones. Lives were lost, and property was burned. The disaster victims fled for their lives with the old and the young. After the overall situation was stabilized, the only thing they could expect for living expenses and reconstruction funds was the compensation for their fire insurance. However, insurance companies made various excuses, and individual negotiations were ineffective. In order to seek collective efforts to deal with the situation, all insurance disaster victims organized the Shanghai Disaster Area Fire Insurance Compensation Advancement Association, elected committee members, and began negotiations, with the support of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Local Association, the Lawyers Association, and the Accountants Association, which organized research and did their best to uphold justice. After several days of meetings, the two sides were very close, and concrete measures were about to be produced. Unexpectedly, the insurance industry suddenly changed its attitude midway, overturned repeated proposals, and refused to send anyone to attend, even attempting to cancel the proposal to issue public bonds that it had put forward itself. Such inconsistency shows a complete lack of good faith. Moreover, it has been found that each insurance company takes in insurance premiums of more than 20 million yuan each year, while the disaster victims are suffering so much, yet they are indifferent. The cruelty of their intentions is beyond description. If the insurance industry insists on handling matters according to the regulations, then the regulations printed on the insurance policy are all one-sided and broad, with a scope that includes a hundred ways to avoid compensation. It is clear that the organization is for self-interest and aims to absorb the funds of the people. If strict intervention is not taken, society will suffer endlessly. The representatives were sent by more than 5,000 disaster victims as the backing of the Shanghai Disaster Area Fire Insurance Compensation Advancement Association and vowed to fight to the death at any cost. Only because this matter is closely related to the well-being of society, we cannot but submit this petition. We respectfully request that you take measures to provide relief so that the purpose of compensation can be achieved. Therefore, we present the following facts and request that you promptly instruct the insurance industry association and convene a meeting of important social organizations to decide on appropriate solutions to save the disaster victims. This would be a great act of kindness. Respectfully submitted, more than 5,000 representatives Chen Zufar, Zhang Shusheng, Yao Gensheng, and 50 others.

Municipal Government Announces the Organizational Regulations of the Municipal Security Office 124

For Local Garrison

Mayor Concurrently Serves as Director

The Municipal Government, considering that after the war in this city, there may be unscrupulous elements mixed in, attaches great importance to maintaining public order. In addition to reorganizing the existing police force, it has also established a security office to ensure the safety and security of the city. The organizational regulations of the office have been passed and promulgated by the Municipal Government. The full text is recorded below: (Organizational Regulations of the Shanghai Municipal Security Office) Article 1: The Shanghai Municipal Government establishes the Shanghai Municipal Security Office (hereinafter referred to as this Office) to complete local security and ensure the safety and security of the city. Article 2: This Office is directly under the Shanghai Municipal Government and is responsible for all leadership, training, personnel management, and financial management of the city's security team, as well as the training and deployment of the city's defense corps, and other supervision and command related to local public security. Article 3: This Office may issue office orders within the scope that does not conflict with the central government and municipal government laws and regulations. Article 4: The organization of this Office is as follows: Office of the Director, First Section, Second Section. Article 5: This Office has one director, who is concurrently held by the mayor, to manage all office affairs and supervise and direct all staff. Article 6: This Office has two deputy directors, one of whom assists the director in handling the training, education, command, management, and other routine affairs of the security team, and the other assists the director in handling the defense corps and other special tasks. Article 7: The director has the power to appoint, dismiss, reward, and punish the officers of this Office and various teams. Article 8: The deputy director has the power to supervise and inspect the diligence, excellence, and shortcomings of the officers of this Office and various teams within his or her authority, and to propose rewards and punishments. Article 9: The Office of the Director has one director, three secretaries, and a number of clerks, scribes, telegraph operators, and staff. Article 10: Each section has one section chief, one deputy section chief, and a number of section members, clerks, and scribes. Article 11: The First Section is responsible for the organization, deployment, pacification, education, training, personnel, regulations, communication, transportation, management, general affairs, books, military law trial, and training and command of the defense corps in various districts. Article 12: The Second Section is responsible for the receipt, disbursement, safekeeping, accounting of money, military equipment, food, clothing, equipment, and supplies of this Office and various teams, as well as the supervision and command of the management of various units and the construction and repair of barracks. Article 13: This Office may establish a number of special affairs officers to handle special affairs. Article 14: This Office may establish a number of service personnel, technicians, and craftsmen as needed, depending on the complexity and technical requirements of future affairs. Article 15: The staffing and detailed rules of this Office, as well as the staffing of the security team, will be determined separately. Article 16: These regulations may be amended at any time if there are any matters not covered. Article 17: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Municipal Government.

Hawer Wang Furen is Enthusiastically Patriotic 127

All Sixteen Yuan Earned Over the Years

All Donated to the Northeast Volunteer Army

A reporter from Dagong News Agency passed by Xiaofanen Wang Furen in Haining yesterday. The hawker had donated the 16 yuan earned over the years to the Volunteer Army. The reporter expressed his respect to him and chatted casually. The hawker sighed and said, "The national crisis is so severe that we hate not being able to kill the enemy on the battlefield. I occasionally read in the newspaper that our Volunteer Army is extremely brave in killing the enemy, which makes people feel a little comforted. I also saw an advertisement in the newspaper saying that donating 16 yuan can help the Volunteer Army to get 200 bullets. I was overjoyed and resolutely donated all 16 yuan earned over the years. Although the amount is very small, it is all I have. From now on, I will live frugally, and I will continue to donate what I earn." The reporter was deeply impressed and expressed it to encourage our compatriots.

Declaration of the National Self-Salvation Association 129

Peaceful Boycott Method

The National Self-Salvation Association declared, "The original economic and social organization of our country has been shaken since it was subjected to economic aggression by Japanese imperialism. On September 18th last year, the Japanese again used force to occupy the three northeastern provinces, the lifeline of our country's economy. On January 28th this year, they again used aircraft and bombs to destroy Songhu, the most prosperous market in our country. As a result, the economic organization of the entire society is clearly in a state of total collapse. Farmers may have land to cultivate, but they have no capital to cultivate it. Factories may have workers to work, but they have no capital to maintain them. Merchants who rely on agriculture and industry for a living naturally have no business to operate and are waiting for death. Bankruptcies are heard of every day. Recently, a large number of Japanese goods have been imported and sold at low prices. The price of yarn has fallen by 20-30%, and the price of coal is only half that of domestic products. Raw silk is our country's main product. It is not enough to seize our European and American markets, and they are also dumping it in our country in an attempt to disrupt it. The Japanese municipal government's newly published monthly magazine 'East Asian Trade Research' advocates that in the future, to establish new enterprises in China, it is necessary to have considerable capital. Their intention is to sweep away all Chinese industries to satisfy their great desire. The Japanese are planning against us so far-sightedly and urgently. At this critical moment of life and death, shall we be helpless and allow ourselves to be oppressed and extinguished, or shall we rise up and resist them to seek self-salvation? We all know that in the 20th century, in addition to weapons and guns, there are also commodities. Killing people with guns is only effective for millions of people, but killing people with commodities is effective enough to exterminate a race. The Japanese are using both methods against us, guns and commodities at the same time. We can only unite and defend ourselves to save the country and seek self-sufficiency to save ourselves. What is the way to self-sufficiency? The positive way is to promote domestic goods, and the negative way is to boycott enemy goods. We all hold these two meanings and specially gather comrades to establish the National Self-Salvation Association. On the one hand, we boycott enemy goods to make them disappear from the Chinese market, thereby compensating for the economic losses of the country. On the other hand, we engage in the domestic goods movement, striving to increase and develop production to meet the needs of people's livelihood, so that China, which is in a state of total economic collapse, can turn danger into safety and become a self-sufficient country. This is the ambition we hold, and it is also the task of this association. Furthermore, things must rot themselves before worms grow. A country must attack itself before others insult it. If our country did not have treacherous merchants to promote Japanese goods, even if they came from the whole country, how could they force people to buy them? Therefore, to boycott them, we must first eliminate internal traitors. This association adopts peaceful means to deal with treacherous merchants, first persuading them with kind words to inspire their conscience and accept the association's regulations. If they do not listen to persuasion, we can only announce the facts in the newspaper so that the people of the country will know their crimes. This is the most peaceful boycott method, which should be sympathized with by all friendly countries. As the saying goes, sincerity can move even metal and stone. A thousand fingers pointing, dying without disease. Do not do nothing because empty words are useless. Gentlemen of our country, why not come and join us?"

Record of the Shanghai County Security Committee General Assembly 131

The Shanghai County Security Committee held its sixth general assembly of committee members yesterday. More than ten people attended, including committee members, district chiefs, regiment commanders, and Xu Yi, the director of security regiment affairs. Committee member Yan Shenyu presided over the meeting. First, the director of the office reported on the progress of the special training class in the past month. Then, the following proposals were discussed and resolved: (1) Regarding how to raise funds for the uniforms, guns, and equipment of the security regiments in various districts, it was resolved that the method of raising funds would be to collect a substitute fee from each household that did not have members in the regiment, based on their wealth: 30 yuan per year for wealthy households and 10 yuan per year for ordinary households. The collection period will begin on October 16th and end on November 15th, and the district offices and regiment headquarters will be jointly responsible for handling it. (2) Regarding how to start implementing the inspection of regiment members in various districts, it was resolved that the office would set a date, notify the district regiments, and convene the inspection. (3) Regarding how to pay the salaries of the training officers of the county security regiment appointed by the Civil Affairs Department for June, it was resolved that the county government would temporarily advance the funds and reimburse them from the reserve fund for the 21st year in the future. (4) Regarding how to handle the implementation of the measures for rectifying the original security funds of various counties promulgated by the provincial government, it was resolved: (A) That each district regiment should submit a report on the amount of the original security donations, excluding busy canal land donations, that have been received. (B) That the expenses and handling of the temporary security regiment should be strictly checked at any time, and only reductions are allowed, and no increases are allowed.

News of Salary Increase for Staff Members of Radio Stations 134

The annual salary increase for staff members of radio stations under the Ministry of Communications has always been scheduled to begin in July each year, but due to various reasons, the authorities often postpone it until September or October. The staff members of various stations, due to the lack of a central organization, have been unable to achieve consensus. This year, since the establishment of the National Association of Staff Members of Radio Stations, the work has been intense and no effort has been spared. The matter of salary increase is particularly urgent. Letters have been submitted repeatedly. Many Visitors to Parks in the Shanghai Municipal Council 137

The number of visitors to the parks in the Public Concession was very high last month. A total of more than 147,000 people visited Zhaofeng Park with tickets, seasonal tickets, and children. More than 153,000 people visited the Bund Park. More than 45,000 people visited Hongkou Park. More than 64,000 people visited the various small parks such as Huishan Park, Singapore Road, Nanyang Road, Yuyuan Road, Suzhou Road, and Kunshan Square. In total, more than 410,579 people visited the parks. The weather was mostly sunny in July, so the open-air concerts in the parks were able to be held as scheduled. Zhaofeng Park sold seating tickets for 13 concerts, averaging 562 people each time, and 4 military band concerts, averaging 552 people. In addition, brass band concerts were held twice in Hongkou Park and seven times in the Bund Park. Many summer and autumn plants have been added to the parks, totaling more than 12,000 Nandina and peony plants, more than 127,000 flowering plants, and more than 40,000 foliage plants. The Zhaofeng Park Zoo has recently received 35 blue-eared pheasants, 13 fireback pheasants, 4 golden pheasants, 3 owls, 3 egrets, 2 deer, and 1 mountain rat, which were sent by Dr. Smith for storage.

The original site of the China Music Association was near Yue Di'an on North Sichuan Road. When the Japanese invaded Shanghai, the association happened to be on the front line and was bombed. It is now heard that a member of the association, Chen, and others plan to reorganize. However, the addresses of the various members are unknown, so there is no way to proceed. Now, for the convenience of contact, Chen's residence at No. 14, Lane 259, Yuyuan Road, is temporarily used as a communication address. In the future, if any members have any opinions, they can send a letter directly to that address.

Pu Henian Gets Life Imprisonment 141

Pu Henian, a native of Qingpu who lived in the rear building of Rongji Zhang Xiaoquan Scissors Shop at No. 825 Dongxi Huade Road, killed his concubine, Wang Xiuying from Suzhou, at noon on the 9th of this month. Wang found that he was broke. After being concubines and discovering his broke status, Wang was intimate with other people and forced him to write a letter of divorce, which he did not agree to. He was also insulted. Pu and Wang had been living together for only more than four months and had spent hundreds of dollars. Before, she had asked him to divorce his fiancee Shunbao in his hometown, otherwise she would not live with him. He suffered all kinds of harm. In such a sad situation, when she used this as an excuse to break up with him, he could not bear it any longer and killed Wang Xiuying with a kitchen knife. The police station has escorted Pu to the First Special Zone Court, and the details of the interrogations have been published in the newspapers. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong presided over the fourth criminal court and sentenced Pu Henian to life imprisonment for the crime of murder. The murder weapon was confiscated. He also declared to the defendant that the charges brought by the police station should be punishable by death. Considering that Wang Xiuying was also at fault in this case, the sentence was reduced. If you disagree, you can appeal within ten days. Pu said yes.

Letter from the Ruifeng Li Housing Association Requesting Landlords 142

The Ruifeng Housing Residents Association of Dong Jiaxing Road, Hongkou, recently had the two neighborhoods of Ruiji and Ruiyuan nearby (with the same landlord as Ruifeng Li) request to join. Their request was granted. Regarding the issue of rent, everyone felt it was too high and unbearable. The association specifically sent a letter yesterday to the landlord Yeguang Company of the three neighborhoods, earnestly requesting a temporary reduction to relieve the people's distress. The original letter is excerpted below: (The preceding part is omitted) Previously, this association sent a letter announcing its establishment and inviting your review. Now, many members have come to the association claiming that during the January 28th Incident, the disaster occurred suddenly, and this area was right in the path of the fighting. Fortunately, there were few residents at the time, and caught unprepared, they all fled empty-handed to avoid the battle. When the chaos subsided and they cautiously returned, every house was empty, and all their savings had vanished. What is even more peculiar is that member Jin Zhezhen's residence at numbers 22 and 24 had its doors unopened, and remained sealed as before, but the belongings stored inside had all disappeared, with losses amounting to a huge sum of 320 yuan. The reason is that Mr. Jin's daughter was to be married in early February, and they had moved here from Zhabei for that purpose. The trousseau prepared was also stolen. It is said that he reported the case to the Harbin Police Station around March 5th, and also sent a letter to your esteemed company, but has not received a reply to this day. We presume you have tacitly agreed to compensate. Now, the war has come to an end, and the residents have barely regained their breath. After the war, all industries are in decline, and it is truly difficult to afford such high rents. We ask that you especially consider this and grant a reduction to help the people of this neighborhood, who have survived war and natural disasters, to ease their burden and hopefully maintain their livelihoods. Regarding the start of rent collection, we also ask for a reasonable extension. As mentioned above, this area was designated as a war zone. Residents who have any savings are all hesitant and unwilling to move back, like startled birds fearing a bent bow. Those who are eagerly returning to the neighborhood now are all poor and destitute people, who dare to brave the dangers because there is no other place for them to settle. We believe this is something your esteemed landlord is well aware of. Considering that Nanjing, Anqing, Hangzhou, and other places were only indirectly affected with very little impact, their residents were granted a 50% rent reduction. Compared to those who actually suffered from the war, how can there be such unequal fortune? After suffering so much, the residents are like dried fish in a rut, struggling to make a living, how can you impose the pre-war market rent? A slight reduction in rent is as light as a feather for the landlord, but the gratitude felt by the common people is as heavy as Mount Tai. If the landlord is generous above, the residents can live in peace below. After a few years, things will surely return to normal. At that time, there will be no need for the landlord to increase the rent, and the tenants will be happy to request an increase first, to express their gratitude for the rent reduction at this time. Although the income may be slightly reduced now, it will surely increase in the future. The overall amount will not be harmed, and your esteemed landlord's virtue of cherishing life will be felt by both gods and men. All of us in the association feel the same way. We will lead all members, work hard, burn incense and express our gratitude at your door. Overwhelmed with emotion, we cannot express our request enough. (The following part is omitted)

Pi Li Dan Cures Epidemic 144

A woman surnamed Lu in Yongnian Li, Baike Road, suddenly suffered from acute sha. In an instant, her abdomen was wracked with pain, and she vomited and purged uncontrollably. She was sent to a hospital for treatment, but was refused admission. On the way back, she was on the verge of death. Fortunately, a Mr. Xu rushed to the Ren Shen Relief Society at 207 Meng De Lan Road and obtained a dose of Pi Li Dan, which was administered with water. Within an hour, the vomiting and purging stopped, and she was completely cured by the evening. Those suffering from the epidemic should seek it directly.

Sales of Domestic Bakelite Light Switches Are Booming 148

As a result, electrical material stores that enthusiastically promote domestic products are rushing to sell them, leading to supply falling short of demand. Statistics on Shashi Cotton Exports for the Past Ten Years 161

Shashi is an important port in western Hubei. Cotton production in the western Hubei region (mainly American cotton) is exported through Shashi. Farmers, recognizing the lively market and higher profits compared to other agricultural products, have been gradually expanding cotton cultivation in recent years. Unfortunately, due to disturbances by bandits, the autumn harvest yields are lower than before, and the export volume has also decreased accordingly. Furthermore, farmers' ingrained habit of adulteration and unwillingness to select good seeds are also contributing to the decline. In late 1930, widespread flooding devastated the province, with 69 counties affected and severe damage to cotton production in 45 counties. The following are the export volumes of cotton from Shashi in the past ten years, according to customs reports:

Year Export Volume Year Export Volume

1921 11,000 dan 1926 652,052 dan

1922 37,000 dan 1927 474,292 dan

1923 190,771 dan 1928 704,420 dan

1924 239,026 dan 1929 558,160 dan

1925 454,086 dan 1930 388,233 dan

Yesterday's flour market, after opening in the morning, generally showed a firm trend in various months. Although the price of foreign wheat was down another three or four jiao, the strong rebound in gold prices and the shrinking exchange rate kept the sentiment among outside investors positive. Buying interest from various parties was very active. Factories were releasing their stocks, and sales in the previous week were very brisk. Yesterday, few were released. Looking at the recent trend, factories, due to the accumulation of spot flour, are willing to sell off, unlike before when they were holding firm. However, buyers' appetite has turned stronger than before, so the market has become bullish. Due to the relocation to the new market, there were two fewer auctions in the morning, with over 300,000 bags sold. As a result, August and September futures were up 7.5 li compared to the previous weekend, October was up 1.25 fen, November was up 7.5 li, December was up 1.5 fen, and January was up 1.75 fen.

Wheat Futures Stable

Grain Exchange Resumes Full-Day Trading Today

Yesterday's wheat futures market, after opening in the morning, generally showed a stable trend in various months. The strong rebound in gold prices had a significant impact on the pricing of foreign wheat. Therefore, general sentiment was not greatly affected by the three or four jiao decrease in the price of foreign wheat. According to market analysis, prices must actually be cheaper, and the supply of native wheat must be sufficient to reassure people before sentiment can turn flat. Otherwise, it will be difficult to overcome the downward trend. As a result, this month's contract was up 2 fen compared to last week, September and October were up 1 fen, and November and December were unchanged. Spot wheat sales were quiet, with no activity. The Miscellaneous Grains Exchange will resume full-day auctions from the 16th.

Silk and Tea 165

Tunchi and Wuyuan Tea Market Coming to an End

Tea Merchants in Wuyuan Pessimistic About Losses

Before the Wuyuan tea merchants entered the market, they were all misled by the high prices offered by foreign merchants last year and expected the market this year to be even better than before. Therefore, even though the banks tightened exchange rates, they still tried every means to start trading. However, after the boxed tea was manufactured and transported to Shanghai, it remained unsold for a long time. The selling price of "Zhen Mei" (Precious Eyebrow) tea plummeted by several tens of liang. Tea warehouses, taking a cautious approach, stopped issuing receipts early. As a result, all the tea merchants felt financial difficulties. Fortunately, American firms showed increasing interest in tea from Wuyuan, and sales of various grades of tea have increased significantly in the past two weeks. The merchants have been able to alleviate their financial difficulties with the income from these distress sales. Some merchants with insufficient capital and unsold boxed tea are still struggling to pay the tea pickers' wages. Even with the recent sales, they still have to take a loss of ten to twenty liang per dan. People in the tea industry often express their concerns and worry about how to recover their losses.

Tunchi Tea Merchants Gradually Closing Down

Tunchi tea merchants were previously concerned about the bleak Shanghai market and the slow sales of boxed tea in Zong. They stopped purchasing new tea from various regions. This month, the Tunchi Zhen Mei varieties became popular, and merchants resumed purchasing in force, distributing 7,000 dan of raw tea accumulated in various tea shops. The market was revitalized. The merchants believe that although they suffered losses on previous sales, the tea purchased later was cheaper than before. The inventory in the Shanghai market is not large, and sales in Europe and America have not decreased. Therefore, they believe that the market will eventually rebound. With this outlook, they did not give up on purchasing new tea due to the temporary market downturn but rather seized the opportunity for future profits. Currently, merchants in Tunchi who have purchased less tea have closed down. About half of them are expected to be completed within this month. There are still about 10,000 boxes of new tea being processed and awaiting shipment.

Roadside Green Tea Holding Steady 166

Yesterday, British and French firms continued to spare no effort to purchase Zhen Mei and needle-like green tea from Wuyuan, Tunchi, Suian, and other areas, and trading was brisk. Currently, the roadside green tea inventory is only about 28,000 to 29,000 boxes. Most of the tea factories in the inland areas have closed down, and the supply has gradually dried up. Based on these supply and demand principles, Chinese tea merchants are taking an increasingly firm stance. Yesterday, the market price for Wuyuan "Gongzheng" Zhen Mei (finest grade Zhen Mei) was 138 liang, and the price for hand-picked tea rose to 165 liang. The green tea market is showing a steady trend.

Sugar Market 167

Raw and White Sugar Trading Slightly More Active

Problems Arise with Muscovado Exports

Yesterday, the sugar market at the Sugar Association saw slightly more active trading. Dutch 24 grade raw white sugar saw substantial transactions at 14 liang 5 qian 5 fen, and Hong Kong sugar at 14 liang 3 qian 5 fen, showing a firm trend. 14 grade raw red sugar was at 12 liang 6 qian 5 fen, and 16 grade medium white sugar was at 13 liang 7 qian 5 fen. Although the volume of 8 grade Dutch red sugar at 10 liang 5 qian 6 qian was limited, the market also held firm. Taikoo sugar B mark was at 16 liang 2 qian 5 fen, HX mark at 15 liang 2 qian to 15 liang 1 qian 5 fen, H mark at 12 liang 5 qian 5 fen, and DY mark at 15 liang 5 qian, showing a stable market. A merchant at a trading post offered several hundred bags of 16 grade medium white sugar at 13 liang 7 qian 5 fen, but traders showed little interest, and the market was flat. Due to the Customs' inspection and re-assessment of domestic goods export tax on refined white sugar, many have been penalized, and there are rumors of confiscation, causing the movement of goods to temporarily cease. Therefore, the industry association convened a general meeting yesterday to discuss countermeasures.

Dried and Preserved Goods 168

New Honey Dates Arrive in Large Quantities, Prices Fall

The previous market price for old honey dates had fallen to around 12 liang, but it has recently seen some recovery. However, new honey dates from Jiaxing have now appeared on the market. The first batch, only a few pieces, sold at a high price of 28 liang. Due to continued arrivals and increasing quantities, the market price has now fallen to 25 or 26 liang. According to usual practice, the morning market added to the退聞貨 (withdrawn goods). The market is showing signs of continued loosening.
