Free Talk

Random Thoughts on Two-Eleven

Stiff, Stiff, Stiff 169

— Zhan Lu

One act after another of a live drama is being performed on the political stage! The most recent act is called "Stiff, Stiff, Stiff."

Wang Jingwei and Zhang Xueliang, over the issue of the military expenses for Tang Yulin's troops in Rehe, and various other reasons, have suddenly put on a stern face! Wang has already declared his resignation, and is extremely resolute, with the meaning of "My heart is not a stone, it cannot be turned." This is called "one stiff." Zhang Xueliang has declared his resignation, and he has no choice but to resign. Ashamed of public opinion and guilty before heaven, why not leave? This is called "two stiff." The reasons for the break between Wang and Zhang are, of course, very complex. The issue of funds is only the overall cause for the break. All of it is focused on Tang Yulin in Rehe. Because of Tang's military expenses, two important figures from the north and south have resigned at the same time. I wonder what Tang feels in his heart? How will the future supply of funds be resolved? This is called "three stiff."

One stiff, two stiff, three stiff, is "stiff, stiff, stiff."

The situation of "stiff, stiff, stiff" will eventually be broken. I am not a politician, so I won't make predictions. I am only thinking of an antithetical couplet with the same rhyme! They are all words in the seventh "yang" rhyme:

Wang Zhang consult over Tang's funds, stiff, stiff, stiff.

Dear readers who like to read this column, why not create an antithetical couplet with the same rhyme?

If there is an antithetical couplet, then the awkwardness of "north of the house, a solitary deer shrinks; west of the stream, chickens crow together" will no longer be unique.

Reputation of Ye Huijun 170

— Sun Choucheng

During the late Qing Dynasty, two civilians engaged in revolution and ultimately achieved success in Shanghai: Li Pingshu and Ye Huijun. Li passed away four years ago, and local people raised money to cast a bronze statue in his honor. Ye has also recently passed away, and various public organizations are holding a memorial service for him in recognition of his contributions to society. The speeches at the memorial service differed from ordinary platitudes. They were all sincere expressions of respect and admiration for Ye, and were worth recording. They are recorded below to commemorate the reputation of Ye in the eyes of the people of Shanghai. Wang Xiaolai said: "I have followed Mr. Ye for more than twenty years, and we have always encouraged each other to be honest and to see things through to the end. Two months ago, when I went to inquire about his illness, Mr. Ye still asked whether the gate installed in Nanshi was sturdy. The Council will be established, and councilors must make it their responsibility to seek the welfare of the local area. This shows that even when he was seriously ill, he was still concerned about local security. He can be said to be selfless and devoted to the public good." Pan Gongzhan said: "Mr. Ye always pointed to his chest during his speeches and said, 'With a clear conscience.' His commitment to the revolutionary cause, from the Qing Dynasty to the present, has never wavered. He always did what he could, never fearing difficulties, and never taking credit for his accomplishments. He always maintained an optimistic attitude. Those who lacked determination were inspired by his encouragement and rose to action. When I was the director of the Social Affairs Bureau, I was afraid of doing certain things and feared difficulties. Through his influence, I moved forward resolutely and was ultimately successful. The old man has now passed away, and the account of his clear conscience has been handed in. He can be said to be blameless before heaven and man." Lin Kanghou said that Mr. Ye's merits can be summed up in six words: "integrity, frugality, law-abiding, and responsibility." He had no savings after decades of revolution. He was always on time for even small banquets. Other things can be imagined. He never promised unless he could deliver, and once he promised, he would definitely do it. The combination of these three qualities is rare in modern times. Qu Shaoyi said that the common failings of people are "greed for petty gains and a desire to be in the limelight." Mr. Ye never profited from helping others. He practiced revolution without any party titles. He was straightforward and honest. He was truly a countryman from Pudong. The fact that Shanghai was able to hold such a memorial service for a countryman after his death shows his achievements can be imagined. Other eulogies are not recorded here.

Photo of Cannons 171

— Ge

When I unexpectedly found several cannons on Beacon Mountain (I only knew its name afterward), my relaxed mood suddenly became serious. I quickly set up my camera and took a picture with the big one.

There were a total of three cannons, two small ones and one large one. The large one was staring straight at the Yangtze River, which stretched like a belt. It was quietly crouching in a ground pit built of concrete, surrounded by concrete walls. The walls were full of deeply embedded bullet marks (the marks were about a foot high and six inches wide), and the size of the bullets could be determined from this. The small cannons were exposed to the sun, with their heads raised, looking like guard dogs.

At the moment of taking the picture, a strangely fragile heart seemed to be shocked by violence, and it kept pounding in my chest. I felt strangely like a spy with an unclear motive, and I was desperately afraid that the enemy would find out what I was doing. But I finally took the picture safely. I was happy! As happy as bullets in a burning ammunition depot, firing wildly in the weeds without a clue. But I was also as flustered as an ant on a hot pot, helplessly circling around.

The mountain was covered with yellow earth and weeds. The summer sun shone universally on it. There was no shade to be found, and even small shrubs were nowhere to be seen. Therefore, I did not meet anyone. However, I heard faint voices and discovered a tunnel next to the cannon pit. It must be very cool in the tunnel. The people guarding the cannon platform must be lying down and chatting.

On the way down the mountain, I still felt like a spy, so I hurried down. But when I stepped onto the wide and smooth street, I felt unhappy, because there was no one chasing after me and no one blocking my way ahead. As a result, I ended up thinking, "What if I really was a spy?" "What if...?"

Eulogy for Lou Junxun 172

— Hong Jingshan

Life is impermanent and death is inevitable. Why did you die so suddenly? Your laughter and words were just yesterday. The news of your death pierced my heart. I was already heartbroken by your haggard appearance. I thought you were recuperating by the sacred lake, and I missed your letters during our short separation. I thought of you countless times, but my plans to visit you were thwarted by circumstances. I was planning to celebrate your return, but who knew it would be our final farewell? A person of towering presence in my eyes is now buried under yellow earth. My heart is filled with worries and sorrows, and what can grass and trees do to help? The building collapses and cannot be rebuilt, and my tears fall like rain in my loneliness and coldness. Fortunately, you have a son who understands filial piety and learning, and your descendants will endure the bitterness and grief. Perhaps the heavens are impartial, and the gates to your grand mansion will open in the future. You were generous in your friendships, but how many people are truly as devoted as you? Floating in the ocean of humanity, how fortunate I was to have you as my friend. I withdrew from the mundane world and entrusted my heart to literature and history. The sound of silk and bamboo music brought me solace, but now it is mournful and heartbreaking. Your neighbors called you a kind person, but you did not care about such praise. I lament the loss of a rare talent for the world, and this is no exaggeration. With the closing of your coffin, you enter eternal rest. When will my tears ever cease?

Unprecedented Marriage Record 173

— Yan Yu

Seven Thousand Five Hundred and One Times

The title of "World's Top Bridegroom" has recently been firmly claimed by a young man living in New York named Hibbert. A few days ago, he celebrated his seven thousand five hundred and first wedding there.

Although none of Hibbert's previous marriages ended in divorce, that is to say, he has never been divorced, he is not a bigamist. Although he gets married almost twice a day, he still believes that marriage is a permanent event in life and hopes that his most recent marriage will be the same.

This is because Hibbert's previous seven thousand and five hundred marriages were all performances on stage. He is a famous New York actor. Only his marriage to Miss Huilai this time is the first real marriage in his life!

Although Hibbert has extensive experience as a bridegroom, he privately practiced all the rituals several times before the wedding. The bride is also an actress who has now given up her stage career and is engaged in the stock business.

Plague Thief 174

— Zhang Puren

After a major war, there is bound to be a major epidemic. This spring, Japanese invaders ravaged the Songhu area, turning it into a war zone. The dead were piled high. After the war, it was difficult to thoroughly carry out burial and disinfection work. Now, in the height of summer and a long drought, an epidemic has spread. The worst hit area is Wuxi. Yesterday, I received a letter from a friend in Wuxi describing the epidemic. Reading it, I couldn't help but gasp in amazement. According to him, a farmer named Jia lived outside the east gate of Wuxi. His family of five was harmonious. One day, Jia's wife suddenly felt chest tightness and abdominal pain. She asked her son to call his father from the fields, as Jia was working as a hired laborer for his neighbor that day and had not yet returned home. The next day, near noon, a neighbor passed by his door and saw that the double doors were tightly closed and there was no sound. Remembering Jia's wife's sudden illness the night before, he became suspicious and broke into the house. He went straight to the bedroom and saw a mother and two sons dead in bed, and a father and a daughter collapsed on the ground. On the side of the wall, there was another person lying on their back. He was extremely shocked and ran to tell the neighbors. Onlookers gathered. After a joint investigation, it was confirmed that the deaths of Jia's family of five were due to a rapidly spreading strain of cholera. However, the person on the side of the wall, upon closer inspection, was recognized as someone from the village. The fact that the dead person died in Jia's house was puzzling. Later, a hole in the wall was discovered behind the厢房 (side room), and it was realized that the deceased was a petty thief who had broken into Jia's house. Unfortunately, he was also infected and died with them. How tragic! (Moved to donate to the Northeast Volunteer Army)

The Eccentric Who Eats Kerosene 175

— Rui Yucheng

Tracing back to the Incident of January 28th, the industries of Shanghai withered and declined. Residents fled in droves. I also returned to my hometown. One evening, I was standing in front of my door with my wife and children when suddenly a destitute young man arrived. He was about twenty years old, looked mentally and physically exhausted, and had a sallow complexion. One could tell at a glance that he was an evacuee. He staggered towards us and suddenly knelt on the ground. He cried out with a pitiful voice, "Please save me, sir! This evacuee really has nowhere to go. It's a matter of life and death!" We felt compassion and brought him into our home. After asking about his situation, we learned that he was from Jiading. He had been doing business in Shanghai. When the Shanghai battle suddenly broke out, his business came to a standstill. Because he missed his mother, wife, and children in his hometown, he risked returning home. However, he was captured by the Japanese army halfway and forced to help transport bullets at the rear. But he was a frail merchant, how could he endure such hard labor? Moreover, he was not well-fed and suffered harsh beatings. Therefore, in less than two days, he was extremely haggard. One day, while carrying ammunition, he suddenly felt dizzy and fainted by the roadside. When he woke up, he realized that he was sleeping in a temporary hospital of the Red Swastika Society. Looking down, he saw a patch of bright red bloodstains on the front of his clothes. He assumed that he had fainted due to coughing up blood on the way, but he didn't know who had rescued him. Soon, after the doctor came to treat him, his mind became much clearer. He began to observe the other patients in the ward. Most of them were wounded soldiers. Only one ordinary patient was sleeping near him. Sometimes, a strong smell of kerosene would blow in with the wind, directly irritating his nose. It turned out that the patient in the bed next to him was a laborer from a kerosene store. His clothes were constantly emitting the unpleasant smell of kerosene. At first, he found this strange smell quite unbearable. But after a week, he became accustomed to it. However, he was eager to rejoin his family and did not wait for his body to fully recover before resolutely leaving the hospital. But at that time, Jiading had been completely occupied by the brutal army, and he could not return home. Moreover, he had no money and nowhere to stay. He had no choice but to beg along the way to make a living. He begged along the railway and unknowingly arrived at our hometown. I expressed extreme sympathy after hearing his story. When he said that he had nowhere to settle down and had become a beggar, my wife and I did not hesitate to let him stay temporarily in our home until the ceasefire, and he could then return to his hometown. Seeing our generosity, he was very grateful and said, "Thank you very much for your kindness in taking me in, sir. I will work as a servant in your house. But there is one condition: I don't want any wages, but I ask that you give me four taels of kerosene every day. I hope you will agree." I was very surprised to hear this and asked him what he wanted four taels of kerosene for. He couldn't help but shed tears and said, "Since leaving the hospital and being separated from the patient in the bed next to me, I have felt a strange pain in my mind. At first, I didn't know why. Later, I realized the reason. So I used the money I had begged to buy two taels of kerosene and inhaled its smell to my heart's content. After inhaling it, my spirits immediately improved. Therefore, I must inhale it every day. In the beginning, I just inhaled it. But after a few days, I felt like it wasn't enough. I even had to drink it. At first, I only drank one tael. Later, I gradually increased the amount. Now, I need to drink at least four taels to feel okay. Please forgive me." His unusual request made me half-believing and half-doubting. But to save someone, one must save them completely, so I agreed to his request. But I thought to myself that kerosene contains toxins. How can he eat it? From then on, I carefully observed him. Sure enough, I saw him eating kerosene every night. After eating it, he was full of energy and would chat with me, just like someone addicted to opium after smoking their fill. Sometimes, when he talked about his hometown, he would weep sadly. After a month, the Shanghai ceasefire agreement was signed. The Japanese army withdrew. I set off for Shanghai. He received the travel expenses that my wife gave him and also returned to Jiading.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Comments

A Few Words in Response to the Three Gentlemen 176

— Buddha

A few days ago, I made some remarks about expelling students studying in Japan, followed by three letters from Mr. Lian, Mr. Ren, Ms. Ruth, and Mr. Fan Xingnan, asking me to reply. The main point of their letters was, of course, to oppose my proposal. Even though they should not study in Japan, they insisted that they should study in Japan. Before writing this reply, I must first clarify two points: 1. This expulsion of students studying in Japan back to their country was done by the Japanese, not by me, nor by the Chinese government. 2. My proposal not to study in Japan does not refer to the past or the future, but to the period after the September 18th Incident until the end of Japan's policy of aggression.

I don't need to investigate whether the three gentlemen were former students in Japan, future students in Japan, or related to Japan or current students in Japan. However, to refute someone else's writing, one must first understand the topic and read the text carefully before speaking. My proposal not to study in Japan specifically refers to the period from the September 18th Incident until the end of Japan's policy of aggression, during which time one should not study in Japan.

Because of our country's own lack of progress, we have no choice but to study in various countries to obtain some relevant scientific knowledge. I have always acknowledged this. However, since the late Qing Dynasty, batches of students have gone to study in various countries, reaching tens of thousands of people, for decades, especially students studying in Japan. However, how much real knowledge have they brought back to contribute to their country? Alas! It is lamentable to say. But we cannot entirely blame the students. The instability of the political situation and the government's inability to make full use of their talents are also among the reasons. In the end, they only bought a few doctoral and bachelor's degrees, which were of no use. The value of studying abroad can thus be generally seen.

Mr. Ren said that every imperialist country is like Japan; they only haven't revealed their ferocious faces because the time hasn't come yet. (This idea is roughly the same in all three letters.) I also think there is some truth to this statement. However, Mr. Ren also admits that the ferocious faces of other countries have not yet been revealed. In fact, they have been revealed before. But when other countries will reveal them in the future, or to what extent they will reveal them, I am afraid Mr. Ren cannot guess. However, Japan's ferocious face has already been exposed. After the September 18th Incident last year, they launched an undeclared war and completely occupied my three northeastern provinces. That's not all; they are also coveting my Jehol and even have plans to invade Beiping and Tianjin. I ask you, can I say that the faces of other countries are so ferocious now?

There is another passage in Mr. Ren's letter that is both infuriating and laughable to read. It is not worth my refuting. I will just record it below for everyone to see such wonderful writing. The Japanese hate the Chinese as much as the Chinese hate the Japanese (How do you know this? Are you perhaps Japanese?). The Chinese reject the Japanese even more than the Japanese reject the Chinese (This is the fault of the Chinese). However, I have never heard a Japanese person say (This is the magnanimity of the Japanese): "We hate the Chinese. We will never go to China. We don't want the land of the three northeastern provinces. We will give up all the Japanese concessions and all rights in China. We will sever all relations with China forever." I don't think the Japanese are so stupid that they would say these words (These words are just something you came up with; clever, clever!). (To be continued)

Progress 179

Science

Electric Light Fishing Technique 180

— Nu

The underdevelopment of the Chinese fishing industry is due not only to the government's lack of protection, but also to the fishermen's lack of scientific knowledge, their reliance on outdated methods, and their failure to improve. If they continue to be self-contained and do not know how to improve, I am afraid that this last glimmer of hope will also follow in the footsteps of the silk industry and go bankrupt. In order to draw the world's attention to the fishing industry, I will now write about the electric light fishing method below.

(1) The Nature of Fish: Place a white porcelain plate in the middle of shallow, grassy water. When the fish see it, they think it is the reflection of the moon and jump into the plate. This is evidence that fish like bright light. Fishermen enter the sea naked, and soon fish come to them. This is another proof that fish like warmth. Since we know that fish like light and warmth, and electric lights have both of these qualities, we can make full use of them.

(2) Setting Up a Fish Trap: Next to the shallow sea, erect four wooden pillars at the four corners. The pillars should be about ten feet high (not counting the part that is in the mud). The pillars should be fourteen feet apart. The sides and bottom should be surrounded by bamboo. The bottom of the trap should be about four feet from the seabed. Then erect four iron pillars to strengthen the bamboo. At this point, the outline is complete. Then, on the four sides of the trap, make twenty or so doors, each one foot square. The doors should also be made of bamboo, crisscrossed like inverted whiskers, so that the fish can enter the trap but cannot leave. Hang a hundred-watt electric light in the middle of the trap. The bulb must be made of two layers of glass, so that the heated layer does not come into contact with cold water, to prevent it from bursting. The outer layer of glass is best to be light green, the same color as the water. The outside of the light is covered with a wire mesh to prevent large fish from breaking the light. At the bottom of the trap, make a hole about two feet square, equipped with a key that can be opened and closed freely. Below is surrounded by a large net. In this way, the fishing trap is completely finished.

(3) Other Equipment: Next to each fishing trap, a fish shed should be built for easy guarding. If the fishing area is far from the city, an engine must be prepared to supply electricity. A small fish transport boat is also an essential piece of equipment, because sailboats are helpless when they encounter head winds. By the time the wind is favorable, fishermen and merchants will have gathered, and market prices will plummet. Therefore, it is more convenient to transport by steamship.

Society for the Improvement of Social Discussions

Replying to Mr. Wen for the Article "Reforming Eating" 181

— Yiyi Hall Owner

Since I proposed the article "Reforming Eating" and published it in this publication, it seems to have attracted the attention of readers and has been discussed. First, Mr. Shuxia, and then Mr. Qixing, have published extensive discussions on this humble view of "Reforming Eating," each expressing their brilliant opinions. I am very impressed. However, the day before yesterday (the eleventh), I saw Mr. Wen's wonderful article "Reply to Reforming Eating." After reading it, I felt that there were misunderstandings in his words, so I added the following explanations to answer Mr. Wen's kind intentions.

Mr. Wen said in his article: "...I think that if there are people with pulmonary tuberculosis or other infectious diseases in a family, then everyone else should take extra precautions everywhere, and there is no need to reform eating..." Indeed, as Mr. Wen said, there is also a point. However, reading his tone, it seems that he misunderstood that the "Reforming Eating" that I proposed is limited to within a family. This view is not broad enough. It must be known that the "Reforming Eating" that I proposed is not only limited to within a family, but also within public institutions or groups where many people are together. It is especially necessary to "reform eating" there. Within a family, it is secondary.

Mr. Wen also criticized my point that "In recent years, the Chinese have been doing everything in the European style," which is also not without misunderstanding. He said: "...Where is the Europeanization? Everything is still subject to invasion and dependent on others. The only things that have been Europeanized are open social gatherings and men and women dancing and all the romance!..." Indeed, that's right. The Chinese people's Europeanization is only like this. How can it not be heartbreaking! How can it not make Mr. Wen so agitated that he even suspects that I sympathize with this Europeanization! How dare I? Mr. Wen is so distressed by the Europeanization of the Chinese, which is truly commendable! However, things have good and bad aspects. The so-called Europeanization also has things that can be learned and things that cannot be learned, which cannot be confused. Mr. Wen asked me: "...What is Europeanization? And what is Europeanization?" This is a very good question, and it is not worth answering. However, since Mr. Wen kindly asked, I cannot bear to reject his kind intentions. I will answer it tentatively, and I hope Mr. Wen will listen. You must know that the Europeanization that I am talking about is, of course, good Europeanization, Europeanization that can be learned. As for the questions "...What is Europeanization? And what is Europeanization?" The meaning of these two sentences is actually one and two, and two and one. Europeanization is the example of the customs and sentiments of European and American countries. The reason why I said "In recent years, the Chinese have been doing everything in the European style" is only because I am saddened by the fact that the Chinese people in recent years have been so diligently learning the bad examples that Mr. Wen mentioned above (but people who learn those bad examples regard them as good examples). So, the meaning of my words is: "Since the Chinese have been doing everything in the European style in recent years, instead of specializing in learning those bad Europeanizations that they think are good, it would be better to reform the eating habits and change to the 'separate eating' principle of one dish per person. It seems to be more beneficial and harmless than learning those bad Europeanizations." This implicit meaning is only because I was too concerned about the space of this publication at the time and did not elaborate, but kept it simple, which caused Mr. Wen to misunderstand and kindly ask me, which is really unexpected. However, Mr. Wen's heartfelt and elegant intentions for the times are truly abundant!

Reforming Education 182

— Xinxi

I am a student and have not been involved in society at all. I am not qualified to talk about social reform issues. However, I cannot resist your association's enthusiasm for social reform, and your association's right to submit articles is not limited to members, so I shamelessly offer my humble opinion.

Everyone knows the relationship between education and society, so there is no need to say more. Schools can be compared to many factories, and society is a large store. Of course, we are all goods produced in factories. No product does not go through the store, just as no student does not enter society. As for our customers? Of course, it is also the vast masses.

Now let's take a look at our sales. How many school graduates are able to find a job? Is it possible to say that supply exceeds demand when thousands of limited students are inserted into this huge society every year? Then how are the 95% of literate people in Western countries placed? This has to be said to be the failure of education. Try to investigate how many graduates of large and middle schools are studying agriculture? How many are studying industry? How many are studying medicine? How many are studying other practical industries? Compared with studying literature, law, politics, and art, it is truly insignificant.

A few days ago, the Nantong Textile School was recruiting in Shanghai, and my brother Lin also went to take the exam. It is said that there were only thirty or fifty applicants. According to the person in charge of the school: "Last year, there were more than twenty graduates from the school, and the social demand was several times that number. Who says that there is an oversupply of college students in the garret?"

One or two months ago? The newspapers and periodicals said that Mr. Chen Guofu submitted an education reform proposal to the Central Committee, saying: "Since the rise of new education in our country, school courses have emphasized literature, grammar, and art while neglecting agriculture, industry, and medicine. This kind of abnormal development has led to a gradual increase in unemployment, creating various unstable states in society. At the same time, we also feel a lack of talent, and we sit idly by and watch the construction industry stagnate." This kind of social phenomenon is recognized by everyone, but who created this abnormal situation? Those who run education should certainly be responsible, but the fundamental psychological errors of the scholars themselves cannot escape blame. This kind of psychology is:

(1) Chinese people have always regarded becoming an official as the only way out for studying. This feudal ideology is still deeply rooted in people's hearts.

(2) Most young people are old before their time and like to make morbid moans, or are self-styled romantic and delve into love affairs, thinking that they can be playboys for the rest of their lives.

(3) They are too self-important and regard practical industries as minor paths, not enough to save the country and secure the people.

Seeing the news that those who passed the higher civil service examination voluntarily returned their diplomas, are some of those who are obsessed with politics also aware? The Chinese political arena is originally a place where a new emperor comes with a new courtier. Do you ask yourself if you have the qualifications to intervene? Wake up! Let's change the slogan:

Go into the real industry world!

Our country has a large amount of virgin land that needs to be developed!

Our country has a large amount of raw materials, and semi-finished products need to be refined!

School Snapshots

Issuing Letters of Appointment 183

— Lin Xia

This is really the education world in China suffering from tuberculosis! How can it be considered a strange phenomenon of School A?!

The time is already August 31st! The letters of appointment for all teachers and staff of School A have not yet been issued! Because the principal has changed again.

Poor teachers and staff who change every half a year are still waiting for their letters of appointment and can't help but feel anxious! Although two or three have already received verbal "reservation tickets" from the new principal, they are not completely stable!

Those who are flexible in nature go to great lengths to ask people to introduce them to the principal again and move around in all directions. Of course, the result is in the hands of others, and they have to run around very diligently! Those who are upright in nature only know to adhere to the principle of "stay if it fits, leave if it doesn't fit" and don't understand what is called activity!

The principal is also really embarrassed. He originally wanted to keep a few good old teachers. However, how can he deal with the superiors' notes and letters of recommendation? Surrounded by relatives and friends, it is difficult to reject everything. The time can no longer be delayed. Finally, he selected two or three of the original teachers and staff who had the most letters of recommendation and hired them, and dismissed all the others. The principal's difficulties were only half relieved.

Fortunately, the upright old teachers would never be so shameless as to make things difficult for the principal. Those who got the "reservation ticket" but could not actually get it could only lament their misfortune!

This is called the education world being more "difficult" than all other worlds!

Fooling Around

Plague God 184

— Bai Tao

Recently, the epidemic has been rampant, and there is unease everywhere. Citizens have been holding peace ceremonies one after another, chanting scriptures and praying, burning hell money and paper foil, hoping to send away the plague god immediately. In fact, the real plague god is not some ferocious ghost or god, but a small, well-known flying insect. That flying insect is the fly that disturbs our peace every day.

Speaking of flies, who doesn't hate them for being too dirty? It is indeed a great plague god that spreads epidemics. This plague god flies between feces and garbage heaps, sucking up decaying corpses and rotten things. These decaying corpses and rotten things are full of countless poisonous bacteria, such as cholera bacteria, dysentery bacteria, typhoid bacteria, tuberculosis bacteria (ie, tubercle bacilli), etc. After the fly is full of these filth filled with poisonous bacteria, it flies to our home. It is indeed a gluttonous little animal. When it sees our food, it stops on it and spits out all the filth it ate before, and then eats the newly discovered food. Moreover, it likes to vomit, often spitting out what it has eaten, and then eating it again. Therefore, in places with many flies, we often see dirty marks vomited by flies on the walls. If we eat the poisonous bacteria vomited by the flies, we will get sick immediately. Its body, except for its two wings, is covered with steel hair, especially on its feet. These hairs are the best tools for spreading germs. It has been calculated that a fly carries between 4,400 and 290,000 germs, including the terrible cholera bacteria, dysentery bacteria, typhoid bacteria, tuberculosis bacteria, diphtheria bacteria, anthrax bacteria, etc.

If an epidemic is discovered in a place, it will spread throughout the city within a few days. The spreader is not a ghost or god, but a fly. It flies from one family to another, from garbage cans and latrines to people's food, spreading that terrible plague. Therefore, if we want to drive away the plague god, we must first exterminate the flies.

The reproductive power of flies is truly amazing. In summer, when the weather is good, it only takes eight or nine days for a fly to turn from a small egg into an adult. Three days later, the newly emerged fly will lay eggs again. A fly, from the beginning of May to the end of August, calculated in four months, its offspring are 191,010,000,000,000,000,000, which is a situation where there is no end to killing. A good defense method is to drive them out of the house, and all windows and doors should be closed with iron gauze to prevent flies from entering the room. But iron gauze is expensive, and the cost of one door is twenty or thirty gold, which poor families cannot afford. Then, cover all food with iron gauze covers, and do not allow flies to feed on it. Killing them with fly swatters or fly traps is also very effective. As for exterminating maggots, lime can be sprinkled on feces. In cities, garbage cans are most likely to attract flies, so garbage cans should be closed, and all waste, such as watermelon rinds and rotten leftovers, should not be discarded next to garbage cans at will to prevent maggots from breeding.

Children's dysentery in autumn is the most terrible. Every year, countless babies die from children's dysentery. This dysentery is mostly spread by flies. Parents should pay attention to the milk of infants and should not allow flies to feed on it.

Announcements

Shanghai First Special District Local Court 185

Civil First Instance Judgment: Yang Ziyu vs. Rong Bo, Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 500 yuan in foreign currency, with interest at a rate of 1.5% per month from July 23rd of the 19th year of the Republic of China until the date of enforcement. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Xu Zhixiang vs. Cao Fanrong et al., Rent Arrears Case (Main Text): The defendants shall repay the plaintiff 240 yuan in foreign currency for rent arrears. The plaintiff's remaining claims and application for provisional execution are dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff by one-quarter and by the defendants by three-quarters. ▲ Lü Shunji vs. Qiao Shouyu, Rent Arrears Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 50 yuan in foreign currency for rent arrears. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant by five-ninths and by the plaintiff by four-ninths. ▲ Sha Tusheng vs. Li Tiangu et al., Loan Case (Main Text): The defendants Li Tiangu and Lao Wu shall jointly repay the plaintiff 70 yuan in foreign currency. If they cannot repay, Chen Da'er shall repay on their behalf. The litigation costs shall be borne equally by the defendants Li Tiangu for five years. ▲ Wang Shunyuan vs. Liu Xuehai et al., Abandoned Inheritance Case (Main Text): The plaintiff's claim is dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff. ▲ Yifeng Foreign Firm vs. Yang Jintang, Rent Arrears and Eviction Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 242.4 taels of silver for rent arrears and street cleaning fees. The plaintiff's remaining claims and applications are dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant by four-sixths and by the plaintiff by two-sixths. ▲ Tan Guiji, rental agent of Jin Guqing, vs. Tao Yumen, owner of the Daxing Steamboat, Rent Arrears Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 773.5 yuan in foreign currency for rent arrears. The application for provisional execution is dismissed. Litigation costs, excluding application fees borne by the plaintiff, shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Liu Shisun, Manager of Shanghai Union Insurance Company, vs. Wang Xiaoduan, Compensation Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 173.6 taels of silver. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Aierjin Sheng vs. Fang Qiusheng, Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 145 yuan in foreign currency. This amount shall be repaid in monthly installments of 10 yuan until cleared. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Ye Laisheng vs. Lao Ji Ni Kaozhen, Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant Yu Duomini shall be responsible for the 500 yuan in foreign currency owed to the plaintiff. If Duomini is unable to repay, the defendant shall be responsible for repayment on his behalf. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ Shi Niangniang vs. Owner of Bei Wanxin Dim Sum Shop et al., Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant, the owner of Bei Wanxin Dim Sum Shop, shall repay the plaintiff 500 yuan in foreign currency, with interest at a rate of 1.66% per month from June 25th of the 16th year of the Republic of China until the date of enforcement. If they cannot repay, Zhu Wenyuan shall repay on their behalf. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendants. ▲ Ji Xueqin vs. Zhang Renlai et al., Rent Arrears Case (Main Text): The defendant Zhang Renlai shall repay the plaintiff 206 yuan in foreign currency for rent arrears. Wu Guoyong shall repay the plaintiff 144.2 yuan in foreign currency for rent arrears. Zhang Chengzhang shall repay the plaintiff 6288.4 yuan in foreign currency for rent arrears. Tong Benxing shall repay the plaintiff 412 yuan in foreign currency for rent arrears. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendants proportionally. ▲ Ye Guang Company, Bai Ke vs. Luo Xing Company, Ji, Rent Arrears and Eviction Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 969 taels of rent, vacate the house, and it is confirmed that the plaintiff has a lien on the defendant's movable property inside the house. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. This case regarding the eviction portion is approved for provisional execution. ▲ A Tasheng vs. Jiang Fuliang et al., Loan Case (Main Text): The defendant Jiang Fuliang shall repay the plaintiff 40 yuan in foreign currency. This amount shall be repaid in monthly installments of 8 yuan. If he cannot repay, Zhou Xiao shall repay on his behalf. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant Jiang Fuliang. ▲ Gao Yihang vs. Jiang Baoski, Rent Arrears Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 400 taels of silver. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff by one-eighth and by the defendant by seven-eighths. ▲ Bai Xiangsheng vs. Zhang Jindada, Rent Arrears Case (Main Text): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 150 yuan in foreign currency. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant.
